Shen Bao National Goods Special Issue

Welcoming the "Citizens' National Goods Year"

— Xuan Wan

Hope

Explore Overseas Markets and Promote Sales in Border Areas

Empty Talk Cannot Make Up for Practical Matters

The disastrous "Students' National Goods Year" has finally passed away very quickly. On the forward track of time, the five big characters "Citizens' National Goods Year" are being written. A new page can be added to the major events list of the national goods movement. The vision of the public must naturally be concentrated in this year, this year, this year, this year with a promising future!

Everyone knows that the past national goods movement was a painful mystery. From the initial roaring "National Goods Year" and the two major national goods years of "Women" and "Students" to the "Citizens' National Goods Year," the achievements of these three years are undoubtedly bleak and dim in our current review. It is a case of doing more with less, but in the process of cutting through thorns and obstacles, we must not forget the people who have worked hard in the national goods movement. They buried their heads in hard work and actively carried out their work, and also laid the foundation for modern industry. In particular, in the past year, the reduction of imports and the gradual increase in exports have clearly told us that the enthusiastic national goods movement has gained great love and support among the broad social masses. At the same time, the improvement of foreign trade has given a bright path to the future of national goods. The implementation of the new monetary policy has given a major stimulus to the industry, which can determine the future trend of national goods development.

Therefore, in the prospect of the "Citizens' National Goods Year," I deeply feel that our future work should, on the one hand, be to determine concrete plans by the industry and strive to explore overseas markets and promote sales in border areas, penetrate into the interior, and, on the other hand, call on all people to abandon the psychology of worshiping foreign goods. You must know what time it is. The dumping of foreign goods has reached the point where it is about to swallow up the survival of our entire nation. Can we still have the delusion of material enjoyment? The recovery of the economic boom requires everyone to stand up and fulfill their responsibilities. History teaches us: "Empty talk is useless, and practical matters are important." We must now move from the theoretical to the practical stage.

Finally, I would like to express my sincere hope that this year's achievements will be better than those of the past, and I deeply hope that the people of the whole country will have a deeper understanding and recognize the current economic crisis of our country. The national goods movement is a matter of the survival of the entire nation, so no matter what the banner is, whether it is "Women," "Students," or "Citizens," its development and growth must be backed by the strength of the masses of the whole country, unite as one, gradually implement cooperation among the same industry and cooperation between production and sales, and cooperation with the financial community, and move bravely towards the road to success.

Advocating National Goods Must Start From "Me"

— Xiao Shi

Mr. Huang Ren Zhi once said, "To get others to do it, I do it first; to forbid others to do it, I don't do it first." These few words originally refer to all things. In simple terms, their meaning is "lead by example." If I want to make everyone love and use national goods, I cannot escape this principle: If you want to persuade people to love and use national goods, it is better to love and use them yourself first. If you want to persuade people not to buy foreign goods, it is better not to buy them yourself first. If everyone can do this, it can be achieved that everyone loves and uses national goods, and everyone does not buy foreign goods.

I have a good friend who has a very high position in society. One day, I saw him wearing a very new foreign tweed robe, so I said, "This piece of clothing must have been made several years ago. It is a pity to throw it away!" He honestly replied to me, "No, it was newly made." "Eh! That's strange! Isn't this contrary to your usual purpose of advocating national goods?" I solemnly asked him this way. He smiled and did not answer. I think similar facts are not unique to my friend. I am afraid that the world is full of them. Such advocacy of national goods that can be spoken but cannot be practiced is a hidden worry for the future of promoting national goods. Therefore, my intention is that from now on, advocating national goods should encourage everyone to start from "me."

Suppose I am a teacher: I should first set a good example myself. Everything I use, eat, and wear, whether it belongs to the public or is private, must be national goods, and I will be a model for the whole school. Over time, the whole school will definitely be assimilated. Otherwise, not only will the words not resonate, but even if you deceive the public for a while, the result will definitely be ineffective.

Suppose I am a businessman: I must understand that selling more national goods is to leave one more point of vitality for the country. For new national goods and national goods that can replace foreign goods, I should promote and introduce them as much as possible. If I only care about my own interests and sell foreign goods widely, or even change their appearance to deceive customers, this is the behavior of a traitorous merchant, not a patriotic merchant, so I say this.

Suppose I am a worker: For all construction materials and manufacturing raw materials, if there are national goods that can be used, I should use them as much as possible. For example, in recent years, workers have been greedy for the convenience of their work and have used foreign pine to build houses or make all kinds of utensils, resulting in the sales of domestic wood plummeting. All of this depends on the workers' advocacy to promote the awakening of the owners.

Suppose I am a farmer: I must eat the rice and wheat that I grow myself, and not eat foreign rice and foreign flour anymore. I must wear the local cloth that I weave myself, and not buy foreign yarn and foreign cloth anymore. I must use the national goods produced in my own country, and not use foreign oil, foreign lamps, and foreign fire anymore. If all the farmers in the country can do this, the countryside will no longer worry about bankruptcy.

Suppose I am a woman: I must clearly distinguish which of the daily necessities needed for clothing, food, housing, and transportation are national goods and which are foreign goods. I must adhere to the idea that only national goods will be used. Adding a foreign good to the family is a great shame for the family. Bringing some foreign goods as a daughter-in-law is not a virtuous daughter-in-law, and bringing some foreign goods as a daughter when marrying is not a virtuous daughter. If women all over the country can view it this way, the customers of national goods will have half of the people in the country.

The Women's National Goods Year and the Students' National Goods Year have become past relics. The Citizens' National Goods Year is the new opportunity for the future. From now on, all compatriots in the country must firmly embrace the determination to advocate national goods, starting from "me." I think the national goods of the 25th year will definitely be promoted throughout the country, the national economy will definitely develop slowly, and the future of the country will definitely be restored. I am willing to encourage myself with this, and I am more willing to fulfill my responsibility to encourage my brothers and children, my relatives and friends, and the public I interact with every day. Let's all stand up together! To overcome the difficulties of 1936 and to revitalize the Chinese nation, we must first start with "me" and advocate national goods.

New Year's Cards

— Qing Qu

Must foreign paper be used, can't domestic products be used?

During the New Year, the liveliest business I see is the small New Year's card, which seems to have encountered a prosperous period, occupying the first place among the products on the market! Don't you see that no matter which bookstore or printing house's glass cabinet is lined with many colorful cards? Humph! If you take a closer look, you will really be dazzled and unable to distinguish which one is the most appropriate and outstanding!

According to a friend of mine, "Although the sales of this kind of card are only once a year, the number of consumers, statistically speaking, is at least more than one million yuan. Isn't this a shocking thing?" I later asked him, "Then, what is the raw material used for this kind of card? Is it a domestic product or an imported product?" He was not in the foreign paper business, but he was very familiar with it, so he frowned and replied, "The paper for New Year's cards can only be suitable if it is thick and smooth. Domestically produced goods are not suitable, and only foreign paper can be used to fill the role. There is no other way. Moreover, the card must be printed with extremely beautiful colored paintings to be pleasing to the eye; therefore, for these two reasons, it is very difficult to make such a thing with domestic paper." I was shocked when I heard these words. New Year's cards are originally very subtle social items, especially the consumption of foreign exchange that only has one New Year a year has actually reached this level. Is that okay?

Therefore, I also thought that the loss of these New Year's cards is not only a pity for the cards themselves, but also for the addition of an envelope and half a postage stamp. In these few days, even if this large number of cards going back and forth is not counted, the number of cards nationwide is probably too big for me to write down. Young students sometimes write a few auspicious words of blessing, and if they are not careful, they feel that they are wrong and still stuff them into the paper pen. Even though they are bought with money, they really don't feel bad! The ridiculous thing is that the national calendar New Year once flew by the cards, and then when it comes to the lunar calendar, it has to come again. This is really too unconscious.

Alas! New Year's greetings? Perhaps it is an indispensable part of etiquette. However, I think it is still too late in this year; in the coming year, quickly come up with a very suitable domestic paper material to eliminate foreign goods and recover rights. Even if it is not as beautiful as foreign paper, you must know that New Year's cards are inherently hypocritical social items. As long as they can express some meaning, there is nothing of great importance? Taking a step back, no matter which generation, everything, can you still take care of New Year's cards during a serious national crisis? I remember that a few years ago, there was a peach-colored greeting card on a certain gentleman's desk. The content was very scarlet and bright, and it also wrote a line of "Happy new year." Next to it, he scribbled, "It's not that you are polite, but that you are shameless;" I didn't understand this reason at first, and the old man said, "The child is shameless and doesn't know that this year is the National Goods Year, so he committed this ugly thing;" This kind of lesson is really worth mentioning to give readers a look.

Viewing Objects and Thinking of People Versus Viewing Objects and Thinking of Country

— Zhao

The weather is cold, the year is ending! Another festive season! Exchanging gifts is a way to maintain friendships. What gifts should we give to our friends and relatives?

Home feels near, but people are far! What are my worries? Thinking of friends and relatives, let's give some domestic goods! If they like sports, then buy Warrior brand athletic shoes or a billiard cue, etc. If they like to read, then buy a Doctor brand fountain pen, domestic ink, and various practical and scholarly reference books, etc. If they love beauty, then gift Butterfly Cream, Samsung toothpaste, Chang'e cosmetics, Triangle brand soap, embroidered pillowcases, etc. For the elderly, gifts like Wuzhou cod liver oil, Sichuan white fungus, Xinghua longan, Hunan lotus seeds, red dates, etc. For children, gifts like Kang Yuan Canning Factory airplanes and various toys, airplane hats, children's storybooks, etc. Strive to make women, children, the old, and the young, view objects and think of people, view goods and think of the country (Note: authentic domestic goods), and be happy in the new year full of vitality!

When giving gifts, it's best to write cautionary words on the gifts, such as "This small gift is entirely domestic, please remember it well," or "Presenting a small gift of domestic goods, wishing you happiness!" or "Presenting local products, no imported goods are offered, please work hard to promote domestic goods," etc. I think everyone will view objects and think of people, view goods and think of the country, and there will definitely be unexpected gains!

A Review of My Plans for the Year

— Quan Jia

I remember at the beginning of Student National Goods Year, I wrote an article for this publication called "Plans for Student National Goods Year." When someone wanted to buy daily necessities, we tried our best to persuade them to use domestic goods instead. Although the effect was very small, our goal was to think from a small scale. For Whom Do We Toil?

— Shi E

Second, published a wall newspaper discussing domestic goods: We originally planned to publish a mimeographed publication with the aim of discussing domestic goods and youth self-cultivation. One reason was that the effect was small, and the second reason was that it was too much trouble. We are all students, and our time and energy are very limited, so we only put out a wall newspaper, named "Weeds." President Yu Xinan and Vice President Yu Bailu are very serious in their work. Unfortunately, there were not many external contributions, so progress was very slow.

Third, established a National Goods Research Association: Our primary purpose in researching domestic goods is to investigate the manufacturing process of domestic goods. On the other hand, we also purchased books on the actual situation of national industry from the association. We have already purchased thirty or forty kinds. Every half month, we review the past work once. Linghu Zhao, Xian, and Ji Yu, who often write for this publication, are members. The association is currently divided into three departments: Investigation Department, General Affairs Department, and Accounting Department, which are headed by Lu Xiangxian and Shen Chengzhao.

The achievements of the past are like this. I think there are many things that can be done in the future. There are many setbacks encountered, and many students, although they know that domestic goods are in this state and that the Chinese people must make a determination, seem to think that buying foreign goods is a matter of glory in their personal lives. When it comes to Chinese stationery, they hurriedly shake their heads and say, "It won't work." Persuading him to buy domestic goods, as if he thought he was being deceived, such unreasonable people are really a big obstacle to the national goods movement! But in general, the students' mentality of using domestic goods has indeed increased a lot.

Time flies, and another year has passed. I heard that next year has been designated as Citizens' National Goods Year. I hope that students in cities and towns across the country will continue to take on our responsibilities!

Hoping Everyone Will Do It

Stop Following Trends, Don't Forget National Goods Year

Shanghai's Difficulties Not Yet Resolved, Patriotic Burden on All Shoulders

Congratulations! Congratulations! But wait! Where does the joy come from? According to common practice, whenever the new year starts, people who write articles always have to write a few auspicious words and words of hope. Today, the reporter cannot avoid following the custom and will also write a few words to congratulate and congratulate, at least to say a few words of hope. However, after thinking for a long time, I still haven't come up with anything. Staring blankly, I looked back on the past. I remember the day this publication was born in the twenty-second year of the Republic of China, which was designated as National Goods Year. The twenty-third year of the Republic of China was designated as Women's National Goods Year. The twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China was designated as Student National Goods Year. "National Goods Year is set, the names are different, ask you what are the results? Scratching your head turns into nothing." Although this is a pessimistic remark from an old gentleman, we who participate in the movement cannot avoid feeling a little ashamed. However, many leaders of domestic goods factories always say that they can encourage everyone to make society more lively, tongue-tied and lips chapped, which can at least make unscrupulous merchants more timid, make fashionable young masters' minds clearer, and transform the hearts of modern ladies and young mistresses. Although we have seen millions of imports of cosmetics and millions of imports of stationery and instruments in recent years, the national goods movement does not seem to be very effective. However, thinking a step back, fortunately, everyone is promoting it, and the numbers are still smaller. Otherwise, I am afraid there would be tens of millions of dollars worth of imported goods, which would not be as much as these numbers. Therefore, only "doing" is the way to go in the world, only then is there a way out. National Goods Year must be done, Women's National Goods Year must also be done, Student National Goods Year must also be done. "Doing" is a great way of self-reliance. Being born as a Chinese, encountering such a bad environment, seeking survival in death, and finding life in desperation, everyone must "do" it.

This year is the fourth year of National Goods Year. Some are designated as Citizens' National Goods Year, some are designated as National National Goods Year, some say Inland National Goods Year, and some say Overseas National Goods Year. I say all are good. Citizens should use domestic goods, and inland compatriots, as well as overseas compatriots, all Chinese citizens should use domestic goods. We are all citizens, why distinguish between each other, why draw boundaries? However, don't forget the following five conditions:

We should concentrate our efforts and cooperate unanimously, and should not reduce our ability to do things with different purposes.

We should be sincere and work hard for the group and serve the public, and should not use the name to facilitate private plans.

We should strive to provide convenience and reduce the burden for the domestic goods industry, and should not cause unnecessary damage to the domestic goods industry or promoters of domestic goods, which would instead create disgust.

We should engage in this national goods movement with a spirit of sacrifice and a sense of obligation, and should not use this to collect money and disturb factories.

We should strive for the universality of the movement and the comprehensiveness of its effectiveness, and should not be fragmented and limited to one corner.

Contributions to Paper Merchants in the Three Provinces of Fujian, Zhejiang, and Jiangxi (Part 1)

— Tian Xuwo Sheng

In June of the twenty-fourth year, I was taking a summer vacation at the Xileng Butterfly Hotel. My old friend Qi Yusan told me that the paper merchants in the Hushui area had been affected to the point of being at the end of their rope and that a way had to be found to save them. I advocated cooperation between machine-made and handmade paper, but I saw that it did not become a reality and was just empty talk. By December, the Shenxin two newspapers published advertisements for paper merchants in the three provinces for a few days, and I thought of this big topic again. The first reason it probably didn't become a reality is that they only wanted the paper factories to buy raw materials, make paper, and then have the paper merchants sell it. This wishful thinking couldn't be realized. Wouldn't it be simpler for paper factories to buy wood pulp on credit, make paper, and sell it for money? Who would be willing to lend money to rural areas to buy raw materials? As far as I know, among the three provinces, Zhejiang produces the most decisive paper.

Although there are many paper-producing areas in Zhejiang, buying bamboo materials from them is always seen as a scarce commodity, because Shanghai materials are only available during the Xiaoman season. They have to prepare enough for a year's use. If they sell it to you, they will lose the raw materials for their own work, so it's no wonder. Calculating the cost, each use of 800-900 catties of green bamboo produces 100 catties of white bamboo silk, with labor costs of one yuan and seventy or eighty cents. The price of green bamboo is no more than half a yuan per 1,000 catties, plus the use of lime, totaling no more than two and a half yuan. They used to sell old-fashioned paper for four or five yuan per bundle, even though humans didn't want to use it. But when burned for ghosts, no one would criticize whether it was good or bad, so they relied on superstition to walk a dead end. Although the number of superstitious people is decreasing year by year, there are still people who want to buy it, because the ash of machine-made paper is black, not white, so it is said that ghosts don't want to use it. However, the superstitious people are dying year by year, and the remaining superstitious friends in the world are decreasing, so their sales are also decreasing year by year, only equal to zero. Zhejiang's paper is all yellow, only the Pucheng area in Jiangshan County, because it doesn't produce lime, has to buy it from afar. The price of lime is light, but the cost of transportation is heavy, so they don't use lime, but use the favorable weather and location to implement their natural bleaching project. Although it takes time, the cost is lower and the output is better, because they don't know how to make paper themselves, and rely on paper merchants from Jiangxi to buy it and make white paper. This method was probably taught by the Jiangxi people. However, in recent years, the sales of white paper have also been occupied by machine-made paper, so the people in the Pujiang area have also become unemployed. The Jiangxi people don't lend money to buy it, so no one makes it anymore. In a few years, it will definitely be like the rice milling industry. When the old hands die, it will be difficult to train a group of people to do it. I have carefully calculated that the cost of collecting materials in Pucheng, transporting them to Jiangshan, and transferring them to Hangzhou is at most three yuan per picul, and one picul of paper per three piculs is no more than nine yuan, totaling no more than 150 yuan per ton, which is cheaper than wood pulp.

Publishing World

On Hu Shi's "Forty Self-Narrative"

— Lin Yiping

Mr. Hu Shi has been vigorously promoting "biographical literature" in the past year or two. He believes that biographical literature is an undeveloped field, and as long as this field is developed, the literary world will add a great light, and culture will have priceless treasures. Therefore, he painstakingly said:

"In the past ten years, because I deeply felt that China lacked biographical literature, I have been advising my older friends to write their autobiographies everywhere."

He advised Mr. Lin Changmin to write "Fifty Self-Narratives," "Unfortunately, he died in Guo Songling's battle less than half a year after celebrating his fiftieth birthday," advised Liang Qichao to write an "Autobiography," "No one expected that such a lively middle-aged writer would only live to be fifty years old!" Advised Liang Shiyi to write a "Self-Narration," and it also became his "dream." Then he advised Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Yuanji, Gao Mengdan, Chen Duxiu... etc., none of them made it. Finally, it seemed that he couldn't persuade them anymore, so our Dr. Hu, who has a "biography fever," in order to "add countable, readable, and credible biographies to our literature," and in order to "provide materials for historians and open up new paths for literature," in what he called "We threw out a few bricks and tiles, just hoping to attract many beautiful jade and gems," he did not hesitate to use his pen to write his "Forty Self-Narrative" for us.

According to the author himself, his "life in these forty years can be divided into three stages, before studying abroad is one stage. Seven years of studying abroad (1910-1917) is one stage. After going abroad (1917-1931) is one stage." But what we see is only the first stage he wrote.

The first chapter takes the form of a novel. Although the technique is not very mature, the author can write out the process of his parents' engagement, obtained from hearsay, without any scruples and purely objectively, which is unprecedented. We know that China is a country that has spread the seeds of old etiquette and teaching. Historically, let alone sons not being allowed to talk about their parents' secrets, even their parents' names are secretly taboo. Some people even resorted to force because others called their parents' names in front of them. But the author in this article actually treats his father - "Mr. Three," and his mother - "Feng Shundi," as the protagonists in a novel and writes about them casually, which shows that it is difficult for those who cannot see through the old etiquette and teaching to do this.

From the second chapter onwards, it is all in the form of self-narration. Starting from his birthday, he wrote until he passed the exam to study abroad. In the narration of these chapters, he can still sincerely rekindle the fire of his childhood heart, and draw a simple outline of his past experiences, the education he received, the pain he suffered, and all the processes of his ideological changes. But after careful review, there are several points that do not satisfy us?

First, the natural environment of his hometown is not mentioned at all: No matter how great a person is, the native land where he first lived has a great impact on his childhood. Since the author was born in the countryside - not living in Shanghai all his life, he should first write about the natural environment in which he lived at the beginning of his self-narration. But the author didn't mention a single word, which has to be said to be a small omission.

Second, it lacks literary flavor: The so-called biographical literature should use vivid brushstrokes and lively words to vividly describe one's past real life. If it is like the author's writing in "Nine Years of Hometown Education," it is really difficult for us to "praise it." Because what he wrote is too dry, too meaningless, we only feel that numbers such as "Guangxu...year...month" and "Western calendar...year" fill the pages, and we never think that we are reading "biographical literature." This kind of year-by-year and month-by-month writing may become good material in a hundred years, but we don't believe that such a work will open up new paths for literature.

Third, there are contradictions in some places in the narration: It is not wrong to use the method of recollection to write one's own self-narration, and to write forward in the order of one's age. It will also give readers a systematic concept. But the author should make his age clear when he is writing. For example, the author "in Shanghai" (page 130) has the confession of "a seventeen-year-old child...", and then there should not be the words "in me, a little child who has just turned fifteen..." Perhaps the author used the words "just turned" to mean "seventeen," but it is easy for readers to misunderstand that a person's age is getting smaller as they get older. In fact, it is not the readers' fault for misunderstanding, it is all because the author has unconscious contradictions in the narration.

Fourth, the improper use of supplementary methods: In an article of self-narration, when there is something that is not worth mentioning directly, but it must be explained to make the reader understand, it can be supplemented in parentheses. But the supplementary should be appropriate, so that people can understand. For example, the narration in "Nine Years of Hometown Education": "There were only two students in my fourth uncle's school, one was me, and the other was my fourth uncle's son, Sishu, who was a few years older than me. Sishu inherited Yu Shuang." (page 41) This paragraph has already said enough; but he doesn't mind saying: "The second sons of Xingwu's uncle, Zhenbo and Yushu, have no sons, my third brother inherited Yubo, and Shu brother inherited Yu Shuang." Isn't this adding unnecessary details and deliberately looking for nonsense? For example, "When my father died, my mother was only twenty-three years old. My father married Feng, and soon after the marriage, he was hit by the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom Rebellion, and died in the war in the second year of Tongzhi (1863)." (page 32) At first glance, it is thought that "Ms. Ma" in the previous paragraph is also his biological mother - Feng Shundi, and when we read "In the fifteenth year of Guangxu (1889), he was waiting for a position in Jiangsu, and his life was a little stable, so he remarried my mother," we can prove that the so-called Ms. Ma is not Feng Shundi, but his father's previous wife. Like here, since they have the same surname Feng, it should be added as a supplement, but the author doesn't add it.

Fifth, the exaggerated momentum is too strong: Writing a self-narration is to nakedly write about one's past real life. Of course, there is no need to hide one's goodness and promote one's evil, and make a false "confession," but at the same time, there is no need to exaggerate everything about oneself too much. For example, the author read a "Zizhi Tongjian" when he was young, and compiled a "Song of the Dynastic Emperors' Reign Titles" (page 74), and thought of himself as "the groundbreaking work of sorting out the national heritage." He published an article in vernacular Chinese in "Jingye Xunkan" and claimed to be "the earliest to promote" "the national language," which is inevitably praising himself too much!

In short, Hu Shi's paragraph of self-narration has had considerable success in some aspects. It can provide many good materials for future generations to make "Hu Shi's Chronology." If we truly stand on the literary position, he is a big failure. Because his self-narration is only "biography," not "biographical literature." I think that the Chinese literary world does not need biographical literature as much as Hu Shi said, even if it does, it is a work that reflects the entire society and the entire life with oneself as the unit, and Hu Shi's "Forty Self-Narrative," which is purely to praise oneself, is fundamentally unnecessary.

National Self-Awareness Movement

— Ye Qing

Mr. Wu Qichang published an article on the National Integrity Movement in the weekly essay column of Dagongbao on the 12th of this month. He believes that as long as the Chinese people have integrity, those who guard the land will guard the land, and those who are traitors will not be traitors, so the National Integrity Movement is a spiritual national defense movement.

This proposition is naturally reasonable. When imperialism intensifies its aggression, those who are engaged in cultural work among the oppressed nations should do spiritual self-defense movements. Otherwise, if the heart dies, a national suicide will occur, and there will be no way to do it.

But how to build national integrity? On this point, I disagree with Mr. Wu and stand in an opposite position. Because his method - adding integrity lessons in textbooks, taking the teachings of the past sages and worthies about "keeping integrity" and "dying for integrity" to talk about, is completely a backward, restoration method, and has no effect.

The reason why some people in the nation do "selling the country" and "betraying the country" is, from a conceptual point of view, because they do not have national self-awareness. This is a very obvious thing. Then, isn't the cultivation of national integrity in awakening national self-awareness?

Abstract integrity teachings are ineffective. And relying on the integrity teachings of the past sages and worthies is to create a feudal personality. This feudal personality is completely inapplicable to today. On the contrary, it is harmful to national integrity. Wasn't Zheng Xiaoxu willing to be a traitor to the nation because of the integrity teachings of the past sages and worthies?

Su Wu's Han festival and Wen Tianxiang's killing are naturally willing to have national significance. However, the reason why they did so was due to the idea of loyalty to the monarch and the idea of becoming benevolent. That is to say, their integrity is the result of concrete feudal ideas, and they have never been for integrity for integrity's sake. Then, the National Integrity Movement should be a National Self-Awareness Movement.

Thinking of methods without focusing on adapting to the times, but only knowing to worship the ancients, the result, in addition to promoting the restoration movement, will never be of any benefit to reality. Thinking of methods without focusing on promoting evolution, but only knowing to go backwards, it is bound to be ineffective and will inevitably be conquered by those whose culture is higher than ours. Isn't the inability of Chinese culture to resist aggression already shown in the past eighty or ninety years?

It is a pity that even today, the need for national self-awareness as a common front is not understood! China's current spiritual "national defense" is national self-awareness with opposition to imperialism as its content. That is to say, the Chinese nation should recognize itself - it is a nation in the world, what environment it is in now, what contradictions it has with imperialism, and how it can be liberated from oppression.

Knowledge is not only morality, but also power. Therefore, as long as the Chinese nation recognizes itself, China will not only have passive integrity members and martyrdom members, but also active revolutionaries and excellent members to complete the great work of national liberation.

However, it is impossible to succeed without thoroughly eliminating feudal ideas and nostalgic feelings to modernize and scientize our consciousness. Therefore, the National Self-Awareness Movement must inherit the spirit of the "May Fourth Movement," determine the past sages and worthies, and absorb as much progressive Western thought as possible - social centrism and its philosophy based on anti-individualism.

Only in this way can we connect our National Self-Awareness Movement with modern culture and scientific knowledge, and only in this way can we resist the aggression of civilized or new barbarism (imperialism).

Raise the banner of the National Self-Awareness Movement and confront imperialism!

Introducing a Chinese Literature Reference Book

— Zhong Yi

—Chronological Table of Chinese Literature—

Here, I don't want to waste time talking about other aspects of literature; however, at the very least, I can't help but raise a few questions for discussion here:

First, the difficulty of studying literature without reference books.

Second, the importance of literary reference books.

Third, an overview of recent literary reference books.

Literature is not just for appreciation, although this is opposed by friends of "art for art's sake"; however, literature ultimately cannot exist apart from its time. In other words, the creation of literature is absolutely rooted in specific contexts. Because of this reason, a writer's birth and death dates, historical background, and the time a work was created, as well as the writer's environment, all need to be clearly understood. Only then can we truly know, study, and understand the writer and the work.

But when it comes to a writer's life and historical background, at the very least, the issues of "time" and "place" arise. In what year was this writer born? In what year did they die? Where are they from? Where and when did they create a certain literary work? Of course, we don't study literature solely to investigate these dead facts. However, in order to understand the literature itself, we must first start with these things. Therefore, many people who study literature often abandon the fundamental and pursue the superficial, focusing on secondary objectives and forgetting the main goal. Why is this? It is because of the lack of literary reference books.

So, literary reference books, plainly speaking, are tools for studying literature. They can help you read books in many ways, and they can help you do research in many ways. In terms of time, you can save a lot of effort in flipping through books, borrowing books, checking, and copying. In terms of mental energy, you can also save a lot of brainpower in researching people's names, place names, and dates. So literary reference books are indeed very important.

Chinese literary reference books were very rare before the Qing Dynasty; they gradually became more numerous in the Qing Dynasty. In recent years, with the advancement of scientific methods and the emergence of talented editors, they have become even more developed. Among the important ones are:

Index to the Classics

Index to the Thirteen Classics

Rhyming Dictionary of Historical Surnames

Chronological Table of Major Chinese Events

Biographies of Famous People Throughout History

Chronological Table of Birth and Death Dates of Famous People Throughout History

Table of Geographic Changes Throughout History

Table of Official Positions Throughout History

Complete Atlas of Historical Geography

Combined Map of Chinese Historical Territories and Wars

Cí Tōng (Dictionary of Phrases)

Dictionary of Chinese Personal Names

Dictionary of Chinese Place Names, Ancient and Modern

Guide to Books

Abstracts of the Complete Library of the Four Treasuries

These books can certainly be used as references for our reading. However, among them, many, due to their different natures and scopes, lack a systematic literary tool that encompasses everything concerning pure literature. Well, the book I want to introduce today is precisely this book, precisely the literary tool we need.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Is There Truly Effective Protection of Freedom of Speech?

— Xing An

Freedom of speech has become a universal demand of the Chinese people today. Recognizing this, the National Government recently issued a nationwide order to effectively protect legitimate speech in order to promote the rule of law and respect public opinion. This phenomenon is extremely gratifying. However, is there truly effective protection of freedom of speech? Based on recent observations of speech, it has indeed been liberated considerably. We were happy that the speech community, which had been mired in dullness for so long, would gradually have hope of regaining freedom in the future. Unexpectedly, not long after the National Government issued the order to protect speech, an incident occurred in Wuxi in which the authorities suppressed speech. How unfortunate! According to a report from Wuxi on December 29th of last year, the Wuxi newspapers received an order from the Garrison Command prohibiting them from publishing news of student petition movements. The newspapers immediately convened an emergency meeting that evening. Because the news recently published by the Wuxi newspapers was mostly about student movements, if they were prohibited from publishing it, most of the space would inevitably be blank. In order to accept the order of the Garrison Command, all newspapers in Wuxi suspended publication for one day on the 28th and issued a statement to inform all sectors of society.

The minimum for protecting freedom of speech is to allow accurate speech and truthful news to be freely expressed without official interference. Freedom of speech is permitted by national law and is a right that the people should have. The authorities' recent monitoring of speech was originally an unavoidable measure under special circumstances. But now that the government has issued an order to protect freedom of speech, local authorities should abide by it. It is regrettable that Wuxi has actually prohibited newspapers from publishing news of student petition movements. Student movements are an expression of the people's patriotic sentiments. Publishing news of student movements is perfectly legitimate and does not violate the law. Why interfere? Does the authority think that students' patriotic actions are harmful, so they don't allow newspapers to publish them?

Originally, protecting freedom of speech cannot be achieved by a mere empty order. Without effective measures, speech cannot be protected. According to our view, if the authority sincerely wants to restore freedom of speech, it should first change its news policy. And the first step in changing the news policy should be to abolish the news censorship system. But in fact, this is probably impossible to do for a while. If there is no other way, then the Central Daily News should request that the party headquarters or the government agency in charge of news discuss a simple method with the speech community. Besides clearly stipulating a few strict restrictions, all kinds of accurate speech and truthful news should be allowed to be published in domestic newspapers. If even this cannot be done, then the government's order to effectively protect legitimate speech is just an empty check, and freedom of speech will never be protected.

Speech is an important tool for saving the country. If the people's speech is not free, it is tantamount to reducing the power to save the country. If the people have opinions about national affairs but cannot express them, and the people cannot know about national affairs, how can the government ask the people to go to the national crisis together in this state?

The Unemployed

— Liang Qiyun

November.

November in Jiangnan has no warmth, no kindness; it has coldness, no sympathy, and the early winter wind.

Tang Xi, whose left hand is infected with frostbite, has become even more haggard these days.

I remember it was summer when he couldn't find a job and thought of Shanghai again. He was no stranger to Shanghai. In 1932, he left Shanghai due to unemployment after the war. In 1933, he wandered to Hong Kong. In the first half of 1934 and 1935, he was in Guangzhou. Those two places were famous metropolises in the south, where he lived by exchanging his own strength. However, when the demon of unemployment followed him like a wind, he was finally knocked down again. He always wanted to get up, determined once, twice... In the end, he still couldn't get up and had to lie at the feet of the devil, gasping for breath.

Gradually, the days became boring and long for him. To relieve his boredom, he often wandered on the street.

Page 18

During this long period of wandering, one day, when he had just stepped into the Hongxing Tea House, he met Ou Jiande, whom he hadn't seen for a long time. — That fellow was known as the "Little Zhuge of Niulan," who had a little wisdom and was good at handling small events, but sometimes he would fail. The ratio of failure to success was about eight to two.

That day, the two of them spent most of the day talking.

When talking about the issue of employment, Tang Xi asked him for advice in the most sincere manner. This time, Little Zhuge did not give him a "so-and-so" secret plan, but solemnly said to him:

"Big Brother, people are not born to starve. If one road doesn't work, take another. Do you still remember that fellow Zhao Songchen? I heard recently that he was appointed as the shipping director of some shipping company. Since he was able to help you with a sum of travel expenses when you came here from Shanghai, I think if you ask him now, he probably won't 'reject you' at the 'door,' right?"

Moreover, he also solved the problem of the fare for him.

"The fare for the cabin (i.e., steerage) to Shanghai doesn't require much money. If you really want to go, you can ask Fatty Zheng of the Guangzhao Public Association for help."

When parting, he also said:

"Man proposes, God disposes. It's not a matter of waiting for things to happen; it's a matter of people finding things to do. Go ahead! Big Brother."

Tang Xi was so moved by Little Zhuge's plan for him that he almost shed tears. That night, he endured it, and under Fatty Zheng's stern scolding and teaching, he finally got eight snow-white silver dollars.

Although Fatty Zheng's temper was fierce, his heart was always righteous.

The second night. —

There wasn't a single person to see him off.

The luggage was also simple. There was only a blanket and a thin little quilt, as well as some daily necessities that were picked up from the grocery store.

He curled up in the corner, letting the Taikoo ship "Guangsheng" take him to Shanghai.

After a four-day journey, he, like an explorer who had found a rich source, cast one last glance at the sea before stepping onto his destination.

The first thing he did was to find a place to live. Needless to say, he visited "Le Yixuan" again. The people who lived there were never surprised by the addition of a new guest. (This association often allowed some poor wanderers to stay there out of regional camaraderie.) Only a few of the most senior mean ghosts there looked at him with suspicious eyes, while thinking suspiciously.

"Long time no see, you silly fellow. You wandered empty-handed for a few years, and now you've come back empty-handed?"

Tang Xi asked everyone about Zhao Songchen's news. Some people shook their heads in response; some sighed; some first let out a long sigh, but ultimately, the phrase "Old Zhao is not as good as before" was often on their lips.

It was hard to find Zhao Songchen's address. However, his repeated requests to see him were denied. Finally, because he pestered him too much, he was told to come the next day.

The next day, after Zhao Songchen declined with a barrage of excuses and gave him a little favor, he was still trapped in the quagmire of unemployment.

These days, his body could not withstand the cold, and his left hand swelled up because of the wind.

He couldn't be discouraged. Every day he constantly thought about overcoming the unlucky devil. But...

Goddess

"Kill! Kill! Kill!" The enemy's shouts were like angry waves in the sea. Gonggong jumped up and looked around. On one side was the sea, and on two sides were rocky walls. There was no way to escape. He shouted, "Followers, rise up!" preparing for a desperate struggle. (18)

Year's End

— Fang Zhou

The sun peered half its face over the horizon of the East River beach, filtering through the treetops, mountain peaks, and many gray and dilapidated roofs in the hazy morning mist.

The wind had not blown for three days, so this small Gongjia Fort lay in peace and silence. But the weather was very cold, and the nearby ponds were all frozen with thick ice. The old hen in the house squatted by the woodpile, clucking and clucking, afraid to go out, but the skinny black dog outside the door hid in the corner of the wall, shivering in the sun, too lazy to get up and move. The open space was quiet and deserted. The thick frost on the green pine branches sparkled brightly in the sunlight.

The New Year pig in the pen was perhaps not full last night, or was worried that its days of bloodshed had arrived, calling out "ho ho ho."

Fifth Uncle walked out of the gate with a weak hand holding a dry tobacco pipe, standing by the screen wall, looking across the old plum tree at the white, misty lake surface, which was also quiet, without a single sailboat.

He put the dry tobacco pipe into his toothless lips, took a few puffs, and wisps of white smoke disappeared in front of him, followed by more wisps. In the past, Fifth Uncle always took his dry tobacco pipe to the open space outside the door to bask in the sun every morning, and whenever neighbors greeted him, he would return their greetings with his usual smile: "Ah! The sun is so good today!" But today, his heart was weighed down by a cloud of sorrow.

There was no more fire in the dry tobacco pipe. He took a few puffs, only to hear strange squeaks. He tapped the pipe head a few times on the ground, shaking off the embers. He stroked his gray beard with his skinny hand, wiped away the clear snot that had congealed at the corner of his mouth, and coughed. A feeling of aging trembled within him, making him feel the sadness of old age and frailty!

He dragged his heavy footsteps, aimlessly walked to a yellow stone by the garbage pond and sat down, watching the clump of light bamboo leaves by the low wall being blown by the wind, shaking their heads. He remembered that the end of the year was near again. In previous years, at this time, people were busy preparing for the New Year: sweeping dust, making cakes, slaughtering pigs. But now the village was still quiet, with no sign of the New Year at all. Only the gloom on everyone's faces had grown thicker, and the worries had become heavier in people's hearts as the days passed by——

"Ah Wu, I've run three times already. This little bit of yours isn't even enough to pay for my footsteps. People are waiting to spend money for the New Year!" Then he slammed the table: "To be honest, I will definitely not let you off on New Year's Eve. You can run away, but you can't run away from the temple. If you don't have money on New Year's Eve, I will move things..." Yesterday, the white-eyed monk's ferocious face suddenly reappeared on Fifth Uncle's mind.

He thought: The debt I owe is not just to the white-eyed monk. There are also food and money, which increase by 10% interest for every month owed. If it is not paid off by the end of the year, the property will be confiscated. Although there is still a pig in my pen, the money from the pig's body was borrowed from the pig butcher Defu for food and can no longer be considered my own. Now there are only a few days left until New Year's Eve. Where can I find more than thirty dollars to pay off the debt? Pawn things? But there is nothing valuable in the house. Mortgage the property? Who would want it in this time of need? Besides, everyone is just as poor and doesn't have food to eat... He couldn't help but shudder at the thought of this, and laboriously raised his heavy and dim head, staring ahead. The faces of the debtors were all smiling miserably at him. Sometimes, he would also hear a series of "Hey! Hey! Hey!"

Terrible phantoms; he closed his eyelids, not having the courage to look, nor the courage to think.

"Dad, porridge is ready!" It wasn't until his daughter-in-law called him to eat sweet potato porridge that he was awakened from his fear and pain.

In the Northern Wilderness

— Hei Ding

In the gray and misty wilderness, a range of undulating peaks stretches along the east bank of the Ergun River. The forests, shrubs, and weeds that are swept by the cold, October winds of the northern wilderness are haggard, having lost their warmth, rich fragrance, and vibrant green luster. The mountains and fields are melancholic.

The deathly still earth is being dominated by the cold season. Occasionally, flying snowflakes fall on the towering mountain peaks, on the narrow plains, on the broad forests, and on the traveler's difficult road.

The mountains are layered on top of each other, so high, so long, and so winding. A rugged, sheep-like path formed of stones, sand, grass roots, tightly clasps the steep mountain walls and dense forests, as if some place cannot be reached. It unfolds stuffily. Whenever there is a clear day, carefree and thin white clouds wander in the sky, but the sunlight refuses to give the traveler a tranquil and pleasant smile, only illuminating the area far beyond the forest. Thus, the traveler's journey becomes a sleeping, unlit street in the night, a deep, dark, and difficult trench dug in the underground layer.

However, every day I trudge on such a path. But I am not tired of the hardships of wandering. A solitary smile creeps from time to time onto my long, clear, gaunt face.

Weary, my aged mood often reverts to the innocent realm of childhood: humming forgotten tunes. I am used to resting on the withered grass by the roadside, gazing at the unfinished road ahead, imagining vaguely. After a while, I look at the jumbled branches pressing above my head. The sky is obscured and far away, only revealing a blurred green outline. So I raise my head, widen my eyes, and part my slack lips, pointing sadly with my hand at the string of towering peaks lying in front of me, counting: one, two, three… After all, it's childish, and I feel it's meaningless, so I laugh foolishly. Hungry, I can shrink my head into the oily collar of my coat and pull out a piece of dry, hard, long, oval flatbread made of cornmeal from my luggage roll, swallowing it rudely. In a few minutes, my empty stomach is filled. I feel my muscles beginning to jump with life, full of the power of great survival. I forget that this is the cold season of October. I forget even more that the mountain wind is constantly attacking my body. I inadvertently take off the black, long-haired dog fur hat from my head, and my two eagle-like claws vigorously grab the itchy and long unkempt hair scattered on my neck. I furrow my brow. I bite my gray lower lip with my teeth. I don't know what I'm doing. I feel like I'm dreaming.

When I am awakened from that elusive and distant dream, my ears hear a kind of urgent and loud machine rubbing sound from across the mountain. The mountains and fields begin to shake uneasily. I suddenly stand up, put the small luggage roll that was placed at my feet on my shoulders, and then hurriedly and frantically, like a chased fawn, stagger straight up the steep mountain peak. Immediately, the shadow of the sun flashed on top of my head; my vision also extended clearly—distant mountains, distant trees, distant plains, distant villages... A train heading to Siberia, spewing thick black smoke, was circling around the mountains and speeding away.

Vaguely, my heart feels a chill, an emptiness.

Movie Star Wang Renmei's Divorce

Movie star Wang Renmei, since cohabitating with her lover, has been affectionate and loving beyond compare. Unexpectedly, her lover, wanting to develop his career but lacking capital, discussed it with a former classmate. The classmate had a habit of being alone, and spared no expense to buy a smile. Wang's lover wanted to meet with him or talk in detail, which could only happen at her love nest. At first, she was unwilling, but after a long time, she became accustomed to it, but absolutely did not have any improper thoughts. People in the flower business saw that he was honest and easy to deceive, and teased him, especially the famous flower Xiao Lin Daiyu, who was the most mischievous. The night before last, Wang's lover visited him at Xiao Lin Daiyu's place. After entering, the classmate had not yet arrived. Xiao Lin Daiyu saw him sitting blankly on the sofa. After entering, the classmate had not yet arrived. Xiao Lin Daiyu saw him sitting blankly on the sofa, and taking him by surprise, stole a kiss from him, and repeatedly called him "Mai Daling," and took the opportunity to sit on his lap. Wang's lover could not escape, and had no choice but to turn his head away, shifting his gaze elsewhere, turning his face to the doorway, just as Renmei stood smiling outside the door. Seeing her lover turn his face, she turned and ran away. Wang's lover was greatly alarmed, and hurriedly pushed Xiao Lin Daiyu to the ground, chasing her downstairs. Just then, his friend entered from outside, and they went upstairs together. That evening, Xiao Lin Daiyu and others deliberately got Wang's lover drunk. By the time he returned home, dawn was breaking. Wang Renmei had not yet slept. Wang wanted to question him, but unexpectedly, her lover actually pointed at Mei and called her Xiao Lin Daiyu, shouting "Sister Lin" incessantly. At this point, Renmei could no longer bear it, and became angry. It is said that Renmei and her lover divorced because of this incident. Another saying is that Renmei ran away the morning after publishing her lover's secrets. What the truth is will only be clear after the premiere of director Shi Dongshan of Xinhua Company's "Song of Everlasting Regret," as the above is a fragment of the plot of "Song of Everlasting Regret," and the so-called Renmei and her lover are also characters in the play, not the movie emperor Jin Yan.

Hu Die's New Work After Her Wedding "The Peach Blossom After the Disaster"

Two Good Films to be Released Tomorrow

"Tears and Flowers" and "Records of Wrongful Deaths"

Since the release of "Madame Butterfly," the name of Shirley Group's Xuenai has been known to almost everyone. Now, Ms. Xuenai is meeting movie fans again with a tragic mood in "Tears and Flowers" (Mary Burns Fugitive). A lonely woman, being hunted by detectives, coerced by bandits, and fought over by men, fleeing east and west, with no security from morning till night. The spiritual and physical pain can be said to have reached its peak. Ms. Xuenai's delicate performance in this film is even more outstanding. This film is scheduled to be released at the Grand Bright Cinema starting tomorrow (Friday).

"Records of Wrongful Deaths" (Steamboat Round The Bed), which will be premiered at the Guotai Theater tomorrow, is also a highly admirable film. Will Rogers, known as the master of humor in the United States, his films are welcomed everywhere, and the box office success is often above the films starring general female superstars. Since his death in a plane crash, movie fans have sighed in unison, and it is indeed a great loss in the film industry. This "Records of Wrongful Deaths" is his last posthumous work, using the most humorous way to perform a very tense story. I hope fans who love Rogers' art will not miss it.

Cast of "Flowers and Grasses"

"Flowers and Grasses" is a new sound film to be shot by Tianyi Company. The cast has been decided. According to director Gao Lihen, the female roles include newcomers Zhang Yi and the stout Wu Yin. The male roles, in addition to Tianyi's basic actors Zhang Zhenduo, Shen Ya Tou, and Xiao Zhengzhong, also include stage newcomer Leng Bo and newcomer Yao Ping. If there are no accidents, this neat lineup will not change.
